## User

This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user invoked the `/adversarial-thinking` skill to determine and implement the optimal Python project skeleton for `target-repos/ttrss-python` following the Phase 1a walking skeleton plan for a TT-RSS PHP→Python migration. All blocking ADRs were pre-accepted (P0: ADR-0001/0002/0003; P1 Tier 1: ADR-0005/0006/0007/0008/0009). The request was to stress-test architecture choices for: (1) testability, (2) sqlacodegen workflow integration, (3) blueprint organization for TT-RSS's API+UI separation, and (4) secret management. After the token limit interrupted the adversarial pipeline output, the user directed: "Resume directly — no apology, no recap. Break remaining work into smaller pieces." The final deliverable was the fully created skeleton in `target-repos/ttrss-python/`.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - **Adversarial Thinking Pipeline**: Phase 0 (requirements), Phase 1 (3 divergent candidates), Phase 2 (critique agent + 3 isolated author agents), Phase 2.5 (convergence detection), Phase 3 (Condorcet pairwise), Phase 4 (winner + runner-up)
   - **Flask App Factory Pattern** (`create_app()`) with `init_app()` extension pattern
   - **SQLAlchemy 2.0 DeclarativeBase** — single shared `Base` class; all models import from `ttrss/models/base.py`
   - **Flask-SQLAlchemy 3.x** with `db = SQLAlchemy(model_class=Base)` — uses custom Base so Alembic sees all tables
   - **sqlacodegen** as dev-only scaffold/verification tool (never imported by production code, AR03/AR08)
   - **Alembic** for forward migrations; `target_metadata = Base.metadata` in `env.py` (CG-06)
   - **Flask-Login + Flask-Session (Redis)** — session stores `user_id` only, never `pwd_hash` (AR05)
   - **Dual-hash password verification** (ADR-0008): argon2id first, then `SHA1X:<salt>:<hex>` (salt PREPENDED — CG-03), then `SHA1:<hex>`; upgrade to argon2id on success (AR04)
   - **MultiFernet** (ADR-0009): instantiated once in `create_app()`, stored as `app.config["FERNET"]`, accessed via `current_app.config["FERNET"]` in `crypto/fernet.py` (AR11)
   - **Flask-WTF CSRFProtect** with `WTF_CSRF_HEADERS=["X-CSRFToken","X-CSRF-Token"]` for AJAX RPC (R13)
   - **flask-talisman** for security headers (R14)
   - **API `seq` passthrough** — every response echoes `seq` from the request (CG-04, R08)
   - **AR07 Hard Prohibition**: No SQLite in tests; project has prior divergence history; real Postgres only
   - **Blueprint packages** (`api/`, `backend/`, `public/`) with `__init__.py` + `views.py` per package
   - **Two-tier test structure**: `tests/unit/` (pure function, no DB) + `tests/integration/` (real Postgres)
   - **12-factor config**: all values from `os.environ.get()` in `Config` class; set before imports in conftest
   - **Condorcet voting**: A beats B (MultiFernet ADR compliance), A beats C (`ttrss/` package name, MultiFernet), B beats C (test structure matches `specs/12-testing-strategy.md`)

   - **`ttrss/__init__.py`** — `create_app(test_config: dict | None = None)` factory:
     ```python
     import ttrss.models  # noqa: F401 — registers all 10 mappers with Base.metadata
     
     def create_app(test_config: dict | None = None) -> Flask:
         app = Flask(__name__)
         app.config.from_object("ttrss.config.Config")
         if test_config is not None:
             app.config.from_mapping(test_config)
         raw_key: bytes = app.config.get("FEED_CRYPT_KEY", b"")
         if raw_key:
             app.config["FERNET"] = MultiFernet([Fernet(raw_key)])
         else:
             app.config["FERNET"] = None
         from ttrss.extensions import db, login_manager, sess, csrf, talisman
         db.init_app(app); login_manager.init_app(app); sess.init_app(app)
         csrf.init_app(app); talisman.init_app(app, content_security_policy=False)
         from ttrss.blueprints.api import api_bp
         from ttrss.blueprints.backend import backend_bp
         from ttrss.blueprints.public import public_bp
         app.register_blueprint(api_bp); app.register_blueprint(backend_bp)
         app.register_blueprint(public_bp)
         from ttrss.errors import register_error_handlers
         register_error_handlers(app)
         return app
     ```

   - **`ttrss/config.py`** — `Config` class with `os.environ.get()` for all values:
     ```python
     class Config:
         SECRET_KEY = os.environ.get("SECRET_KEY", "")
         SQLALCHEMY_DATABASE_URI = os.environ.get("DATABASE_URL", "")
         FEED_CRYPT_KEY = os.environ.get("FEED_CRYPT_KEY", "").encode()
         SESSION_TYPE = "redis"
         SESSION_REDIS = Redis.from_url(os.environ.get("REDIS_URL", "redis://localhost:6379/0"))
         SESSION_USE_SIGNER = True
         SESSION_COOKIE_HTTPONLY = True
         SESSION_COOKIE_SAMESITE = "Lax"
         SESSION_COOKIE_LIFETIME = int(os.environ.get("SESSION_COOKIE_LIFETIME", "86400"))
         WTF_CSRF_ENABLED = True
         WTF_CSRF_HEADERS = ["X-CSRFToken", "X-CSRF-Token"]
         SQLALCHEMY_ENGINE_OPTIONS = {"pool_pre_ping": True}
     ```

   - **`ttrss/extensions.py`** — all extensions without app; `db = SQLAlchemy(model_class=Base)` to share single metadata; lazy `user_loader` import (AR02):
     ```python
     from ttrss.models.base import Base
     db = SQLAlchemy(model_class=Base)
     login_manager = LoginManager()
     sess = Session(); csrf = CSRFProtect(); talisman = Talisman()
     
     @login_manager.user_loader
     def load_user(user_id: str):
         from ttrss.models.user import TtRssUser
         return db.session.get(TtRssUser, int(user_id))
     ```

   - **`ttrss/errors.py`** — 400/401/403/404/500 handlers; JSON for `/api/` paths, plain text otherwise

   - **`ttrss/models/base.py`** — single `class Base(DeclarativeBase): pass`

   - **`ttrss/models/__init__.py`** — imports all 10 model classes for mapper registration; re-exports `Base`

   - **`ttrss/models/user.py`** — `TtRssUser(UserMixin, Base)` with id, login, pwd_hash, access_level, last_login, salt, otp_enabled, created_time

   - **`ttrss/models/feed.py`** — `TtRssFeed(Base)` with Fernet `auth_pass` property:
     ```python
     @property
     def auth_pass(self) -> Optional[str]:
         if self._auth_pass is None: return None
         from ttrss.crypto.fernet import fernet_decrypt
         return fernet_decrypt(self._auth_pass)
     
     @auth_pass.setter
     def auth_pass(self, value: Optional[str]) -> None:
         if value is None: self._auth_pass = None
         else:
             from ttrss.crypto.fernet import fernet_encrypt
             self._auth_pass = fernet_encrypt(value)
     ```

   - **`ttrss/models/category.py`** — `TtRssFeedCategory(Base)`: id, owner_uid, title, parent_cat, order_id
   - **`ttrss/models/entry.py`** — `TtRssEntry(Base)`: id, title, link, content, content_hash, updated, date_entered, guid, num_comments, author
   - **`ttrss/models/user_entry.py`** — `TtRssUserEntry(Base)`: int_id, ref_id, owner_uid, feed_id, unread, marked, published, score, tag_cache, label_cache, last_read, note, orig_feed_id
   - **`ttrss/models/label.py`** — `TtRssLabel2(Base)` + `TtRssUserLabel2(Base)` (co-located tightly coupled pair)
   - **`ttrss/models/tag.py`** — `TtRssTag(Base)`: id, owner_uid, tag_name, post_int_id
   - **`ttrss/models/enclosure.py`** — `TtRssEnclosure(Base)`: id, post_id, content_url, content_type, title, duration, width, height
   - **`ttrss/models/version.py`** — `TtRssVersion(Base)`: schema_version (primary_key); single-column table for schema version tracking (CG-01)

   - **`ttrss/auth/password.py`** — dual-hash verification (ADR-0008, R10, AR04, CG-03):
     ```python
     def verify_password(stored_hash: str, password: str) -> bool:
         if stored_hash.startswith("$argon2"):
             try: return _ph.verify(stored_hash, password)
             except (VerifyMismatchError, InvalidHashError): return False
         if stored_hash.startswith("SHA1X:"):
             parts = stored_hash.split(":", 2)
             if len(parts) != 3: return False
             _, salt, digest = parts
             # CG-03: salt PREPENDED — sha1(salt + password)
             expected = hashlib.sha1((salt + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
             return expected == digest
         if stored_hash.startswith("SHA1:"):
             digest = stored_hash[5:]
             expected = hashlib.sha1(password.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
             return expected == digest
         return False
     
     def hash_password(password: str) -> str:
         return _ph.hash(password)  # always argon2id (AR04)
     
     def needs_upgrade(stored_hash: str) -> bool:
         return not stored_hash.startswith("$argon2")
     ```

   - **`ttrss/auth/session.py`** — stub module documenting AR05 (no pwd_hash in session)

   - **`ttrss/crypto/fernet.py`** — `fernet_encrypt()`/`fernet_decrypt()` via `current_app.config["FERNET"]` (AR11):
     ```python
     def fernet_encrypt(plaintext: str) -> str:
         f = current_app.config["FERNET"]
         if f is None: raise RuntimeError("FERNET not configured...")
         return f.encrypt(plaintext.encode("utf-8")).decode("ascii")
     
     def fernet_decrypt(token: str) -> str:
         f = current_app.config["FERNET"]
         if f is None: raise RuntimeError("FERNET not configured...")
         return f.decrypt(token.encode("ascii")).decode("utf-8")
     ```

   - **`ttrss/blueprints/api/views.py`** — `api_bp = Blueprint("api", __name__, url_prefix="/api")`; single dispatch route `GET/POST /api/`; `_seq()` extracts and echoes seq (CG-04); `_handle_login()` does argon2id verify, SHA1 upgrade, stores only `session["user_id"]` (AR05):
     ```python
     def _handle_login(data: dict, seq: int):
         user = db.session.scalars(db.select(TtRssUser).where(TtRssUser.login == username)).first()
         if not user or not verify_password(user.pwd_hash, password):
             return _err(seq, "LOGIN_ERROR")
         if needs_upgrade(user.pwd_hash):
             user.pwd_hash = hash_password(password); db.session.commit()
         login_user(user)
         session["user_id"] = user.id  # AR05: user_id only
         return _ok(seq, {"session_id": getattr(session, "sid", ""), "api_level": 8})
     ```

   - **`ttrss/blueprints/api/__init__.py`** — `from ttrss.blueprints.api.views import api_bp`
   - **`ttrss/blueprints/backend/views.py`** — Phase 1a stub; `@backend_bp.post("/backend.php")` `@login_required`; CSRF enforced globally
   - **`ttrss/blueprints/public/views.py`** — `@public_bp.get("/")` health check stub

   - **`alembic/env.py`** — imports `ttrss.models` for mapper registration; `target_metadata = Base.metadata`; reads `DATABASE_URL` from env (CG-06, R03):

   - **`alembic/script.py.mako`** — standard Alembic revision template

     _TEST_FERNET_KEY = Fernet.generate_key().decode()

     ```

   - **`tests/unit/test_password.py`** — pure function tests; includes CG-03 regression (salt-prepended vs salt-appended must not match); tests argon2id, SHA1X, SHA1, unknown format rejection
   - **`tests/unit/test_crypto.py`** — Fernet round-trip with minimal Flask app context; tests unicode, wrong key raises `InvalidToken`, None FERNET raises `RuntimeError`
   - **`tests/integration/test_api_login.py`** — integration tests for login/isLoggedIn; asserts seq echo, AR05 (no pwd_hash in response), logout, unknown user rejection

4. Errors and fixes:
   - **Token limit hit mid-implementation**: The adversarial thinking pipeline and planning phase consumed the output token budget before files were created. User instructed: "Resume directly — no apology, no recap. Break remaining work into smaller pieces." Fixed by splitting all file creation into 5 parallel agent batches.
   - **Dual DeclarativeBase risk (A-NC-02/03)**: Original Candidate A had `_generated/` directory with its own Base, plus a second Base in extensions.py. Fixed by removing `_generated/` from production code entirely, establishing single `Base` in `ttrss/models/base.py`, and using `SQLAlchemy(model_class=Base)` in extensions.py.
   - **SQLite in unit tests (B-NC-01)**: Candidate B's original design used SQLite in-memory for AuthService unit tests — direct violation of AR07 (prior divergence history). Fixed by removing SQLite entirely; pure function tests (password, crypto) need no DB; integration tests use real Postgres.
   - **Premature service layer (B-NC-02)**: Candidate B had `AuthService` and `CryptoService` classes. Fixed by replacing with module-level functions in `auth.py` and `crypto.py` (AR10 compliance).
   - **Monolithic models.py (C-NC-01)**: Candidate C had all 10 models in a single file. Fixed by splitting into `models/` package with one file per domain table (AR12 compliance).
   - **ttrss_version missing (CG-01)**: All three original candidates omitted this 10th required model. Fixed by adding `ttrss/models/version.py` with `TtRssVersion(Base)`.
   - **SHA1 salt order (CG-03)**: None specified the concatenation order. Fixed explicitly: `hashlib.sha1((salt + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()` — salt prepended; added regression test that salt-appended hash must NOT verify.
   - **seq passthrough (CG-04)**: None addressed API seq echoing. Fixed in `_seq()` helper and all response paths.
   - **/public/ blueprint absent (B-NC-06, C-NC-06)**: Fixed by adding `ttrss/blueprints/public/` package.
   - **CSRF on AJAX RPC (CG-05)**: Fixed via `WTF_CSRF_HEADERS = ["X-CSRFToken", "X-CSRF-Token"]` in Config.
   - **Alembic env.py metadata (CG-06)**: Fixed by `target_metadata = Base.metadata` in `alembic/env.py`.
   - **Flask-Session config (CG-07)**: Fixed by explicit `SESSION_TYPE`, `SESSION_REDIS`, `SESSION_USE_SIGNER=True` in Config.
   - **Fernet inline in model code (AR11)**: All three candidates risked instantiating Fernet inside model properties. Fixed: `MultiFernet` built once in `create_app()`, stored in `app.config["FERNET"]`, accessed via `current_app.config["FERNET"]` in `crypto/fernet.py` helpers only.

5. Problem Solving:
   - **Walking skeleton vs over-engineering tension**: Resolved by using Solution A (blueprint packages, `ttrss/` name, MultiFernet) but keeping models as hand-written files (not sqlacodegen output) and keeping `create_app()` as the sole orchestration point.
   - **Import timing for Config class attributes**: Resolved by setting env vars at module level in conftest.py before any ttrss imports, plus `create_app(test_config=dict)` override parameter.
   - **Circular import prevention**: `extensions.py` lazy-imports models inside `user_loader`; blueprints imported inside `create_app()` body; model files only import from `ttrss.models.base` (no back-references to extensions).
   - **sqlacodegen vs hand-written models coexistence**: sqlacodegen output goes to `scripts/sqlacodegen_reference/` (gitignored for .py files, never in ttrss/ import path); `gen_models.sh` documents the comparison workflow.

    12→def create_app(test_config: dict | None = None) -> Flask:
    13→    """
    14→    Application factory (R01).
    15→    test_config: optional dict to override config for tests (e.g. SQLALCHEMY_DATABASE_URI).
    16→    """
    17→    app = Flask(__name__)
    18→    app.config.from_object("ttrss.config.Config")
    19→
    20→    if test_config is not None:
    21→        app.config.from_mapping(test_config)
    22→
    23→    # Fernet — instantiated ONCE here, stored in app.config (R11, ADR-0009, AR11).
    24→    # MultiFernet supports key rotation per ADR-0009.
    25→    raw_key: bytes = app.config.get("FEED_CRYPT_KEY", b"")
    26→    if raw_key:
    27→        app.config["FERNET"] = MultiFernet([Fernet(raw_key)])
    28→    else:
    29→        app.config["FERNET"] = None  # will fail at encrypt/decrypt; acceptable for skeleton
    30→
    31→    # Extensions — init_app pattern avoids circular imports (AR02)
    32→    from ttrss.extensions import db, login_manager, sess, csrf, talisman
    33→    db.init_app(app)
    34→    login_manager.init_app(app)
    35→    sess.init_app(app)
    36→    csrf.init_app(app)
    37→    talisman.init_app(app, content_security_policy=False)
    38→
    39→    # Blueprints — imported inside factory to prevent circular imports (AR02)

    41→    from ttrss.blueprints.backend import backend_bp
    42→    from ttrss.blueprints.public import public_bp
    43→    app.register_blueprint(api_bp)
    44→    app.register_blueprint(backend_bp)
    45→    app.register_blueprint(public_bp)
    46→

    48→    register_error_handlers(app)
    49→
    50→    return app

**Tool Call: cat tests/unit/test_password.py**
Status: Completed

Terminal:
```
"""
Pure function tests for ttrss.auth.password (ADR-0008, R10, AR04).
No database required — these functions operate on strings only.
AR07-compliant: AR07 prohibits SQLite as DB substitute, not the absence of a DB
when none is genuinely needed.

CG-03 regression: SHA1X salt MUST be prepended (sha1(salt+password)), not appended.
"""
import hashlib

from ttrss.auth.password import hash_password, needs_upgrade, verify_password


def test_hash_password_produces_argon2id():
    h = hash_password("testpassword")
    assert h.startswith("$argon2id$"), "hash_password must produce argon2id hash (AR04)"


def test_verify_argon2id_correct():
    h = hash_password("correcthorse")
    assert verify_password(h, "correcthorse") is True


def test_verify_argon2id_wrong():
    h = hash_password("correcthorse")
    assert verify_password(h, "wrongpassword") is False


def test_verify_sha1x_salt_prepended():
    """CG-03: SHA1X — salt MUST be prepended: sha1(salt + password)."""
    salt = "abc123salt"
    password = "hunter2"
    correct_digest = hashlib.sha1((salt + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    stored = f"SHA1X:{salt}:{correct_digest}"
    assert verify_password(stored, password) is True


def test_verify_sha1x_salt_not_appended():
    """Regression: salt appended instead of prepended MUST NOT verify (CG-03)."""
    salt = "abc123salt"
    password = "hunter2"
    wrong_digest = hashlib.sha1((password + salt).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    stored = f"SHA1X:{salt}:{wrong_digest}"
    assert verify_password(stored, password) is False, (
        "Salt-appended hash must NOT verify — salt must be prepended (CG-03)"
    )


def test_verify_sha1x_wrong_password():
    salt = "s"
    password = "correct"
    digest = hashlib.sha1((salt + password).encode()).hexdigest()
    stored = f"SHA1X:{salt}:{digest}"
    assert verify_password(stored, "wrong") is False


def test_verify_sha1_unsalted():
    """Legacy unsalted SHA1 (older TT-RSS versions)."""
    password = "legacy"
    digest = hashlib.sha1(password.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    stored = f"SHA1:{digest}"
    assert verify_password(stored, password) is True


def test_verify_sha1_unsalted_wrong():
    password = "legacy"
    digest = hashlib.sha1(password.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    stored = f"SHA1:{digest}"
    assert verify_password(stored, "wrong") is False


def test_needs_upgrade_sha1x_returns_true():
    salt = "s"
    digest = hashlib.sha1(("s" + "p").encode()).hexdigest()
    assert needs_upgrade(f"SHA1X:{salt}:{digest}") is True


def test_needs_upgrade_argon2id_returns_false():
    h = hash_password("p")
    assert needs_upgrade(h) is False


def test_verify_unknown_format_rejected():
    assert verify_password("PLAINTEXT:password", "password") is False
    assert verify_password("md5:5f4dcc3b5aa765d61d8327deb882cf99", "password") is False
    assert verify_password("", "password") is False
```

```
"""
Test fixtures (R15, AR07, specs/12-testing-strategy.md).

AR07 (HARD PROHIBITION): No SQLite in tests.
This project has explicit prior history of mock/prod divergence that masked a
broken migration. All ORM-touching tests use real Postgres via docker-compose.test.yml.

Setup:
  docker compose -f docker-compose.test.yml up -d
  export TEST_DATABASE_URL=postgresql://ttrss_test:ttrss_test@localhost:5433/ttrss_test
  export TEST_REDIS_URL=redis://localhost:6380/1
  pytest
"""
import os

from cryptography.fernet import Fernet

# Generate a stable test Fernet key before importing ttrss modules.
# Config class attributes are evaluated at import time, so env vars must be set first.
_TEST_FERNET_KEY = Fernet.generate_key().decode()

# Set test env vars before any ttrss import.
# setdefault preserves values already set in the environment (e.g. from CI).
os.environ.setdefault("SECRET_KEY", "test-secret-key-not-for-production")
os.environ.setdefault("FEED_CRYPT_KEY", _TEST_FERNET_KEY)
os.environ.setdefault(
    "DATABASE_URL",
    os.environ.get(
        "TEST_DATABASE_URL",
        "postgresql://ttrss_test:ttrss_test@localhost:5433/ttrss_test",
    ),
)
os.environ.setdefault(
    "REDIS_URL",
    os.environ.get("TEST_REDIS_URL", "redis://localhost:6380/1"),
)

import pytest  # noqa: E402

from ttrss import create_app  # noqa: E402
from ttrss.extensions import db as _db  # noqa: E402


@pytest.fixture(scope="session")
def app():
    """
    Session-scoped Flask app for integration tests.
    Uses real Postgres (TEST_DATABASE_URL) — no SQLite (AR07).
    """
    test_db_url = os.environ.get(
        "TEST_DATABASE_URL",
        os.environ.get("DATABASE_URL", ""),
    )
    if not test_db_url or "sqlite" in test_db_url:
        pytest.skip(
            "TEST_DATABASE_URL must point to a real Postgres test database (AR07). "
            "Run: docker compose -f docker-compose.test.yml up -d"
        )

    test_redis_url = os.environ.get("TEST_REDIS_URL", "redis://localhost:6380/1")

    from redis import Redis

    application = create_app(
        {
            "TESTING": True,
            "SQLALCHEMY_DATABASE_URI": test_db_url,
            "SESSION_REDIS": Redis.from_url(test_redis_url),
            "FEED_CRYPT_KEY": _TEST_FERNET_KEY.encode(),
            "WTF_CSRF_ENABLED": False,  # disabled in test client; CSRF tested separately
        }
    )

    with application.app_context():
        _db.create_all()
        yield application
        _db.drop_all()


@pytest.fixture()
def client(app):
    return app.test_client()


@pytest.fixture()
def db_session(app):
    with app.app_context():
        yield _db.session
        _db.session.rollback()
```

**Tool Call: Read target-repos/ttrss-python/ttrss/auth/password.py**
Status: Completed

```
     1→"""
     2→Dual-hash password verification (ADR-0008, R10, AR04).
     3→
     4→Verification order:
     5→1. argon2id  — modern hash; new passwords and upgraded legacy passwords
     6→2. SHA1X:<salt>:<hex>  — legacy salted SHA1 (TT-RSS PHP format)
     7→3. SHA1:<hex>          — legacy unsalted SHA1 (older TT-RSS versions)
     8→
     9→CG-03: SHA1X salt is PREPENDED — sha1(salt + password), NOT sha1(password + salt).
    10→AR04: SHA1 is verify-only. All new/upgraded hashes use argon2id exclusively.
    11→"""
    12→import hashlib
    13→
    14→from argon2 import PasswordHasher
    15→from argon2.exceptions import InvalidHashError, VerifyMismatchError
    16→
    17→_ph = PasswordHasher()  # argon2id by default in argon2-cffi
    18→
    19→
    20→def hash_password(password: str) -> str:
    21→    """Hash a new password with argon2id. Never SHA1 for new passwords (AR04)."""
    22→    return _ph.hash(password)
    23→
    24→
    25→def verify_password(stored_hash: str, password: str) -> bool:
    26→    """
    27→    Verify password against stored hash.
    28→    Returns True if valid, False otherwise.
    29→    Does not modify the stored hash — call upgrade_hash() after a successful SHA1 verify.
    30→
    31→    SHA1X salt is extracted from the stored_hash string itself (not passed separately).
    32→    CG-03: sha1(SALT + password) — salt is PREPENDED.
    33→    """
    34→    if stored_hash.startswith("$argon2"):
    35→        try:
    36→            return _ph.verify(stored_hash, password)
    37→        except (VerifyMismatchError, InvalidHashError):
    38→            return False
    39→
    40→    if stored_hash.startswith("SHA1X:"):
    41→        # Format: SHA1X:<salt>:<hex_digest>
    42→        parts = stored_hash.split(":", 2)
    43→        if len(parts) != 3:
    44→            return False
    45→        _, salt, digest = parts
    46→        # CG-03: salt PREPENDED — sha1(salt + password)
    47→        expected = hashlib.sha1((salt + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    48→        return expected == digest
    49→
    50→    if stored_hash.startswith("SHA1:"):
    51→        # Unsalted SHA1 (older TT-RSS)
    52→        digest = stored_hash[5:]
    53→        expected = hashlib.sha1(password.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    54→        return expected == digest
    55→
    56→    return False  # unknown hash format — reject
    57→
    58→
    59→def needs_upgrade(stored_hash: str) -> bool:
    60→    """Return True if the stored hash should be upgraded to argon2id (ADR-0008)."""
    61→    return not stored_hash.startswith("$argon2")
    62→

<system-reminder>

But you MUST refuse to improve or augment the code. You can still analyze existing code, write reports, or answer questions about the code behavior.
</system-reminder>
```

**Tool Call: Read target-repos/ttrss-python/ttrss/blueprints/api/views.py**
Status: Completed

```
     1→"""
     2→TT-RSS REST API (/api/ — equivalent to PHP api/index.php).
     3→
     4→Protocol (spec/03-api-routing.md, R08, R09):
     5→  POST or GET /api/ with JSON body (or query params for GET).
     6→  Response envelope: {"seq": N, "status": 0|1, "content": {...}}
     7→  seq MUST be echoed from the request in every response (CG-04).
     8→  API level: 8.
     9→
    10→Auth (ADR-0007, ADR-0008, R07, AR05):
    11→  Login stores user_id in Redis session only — never pwd_hash (AR05).
    12→  Legacy SHA1 hashes are upgraded to argon2id on first successful login (ADR-0008).
    13→"""
    14→from flask import Blueprint, jsonify, session
    15→from flask_login import current_user, login_user, logout_user
    16→
    17→from ttrss.auth.password import hash_password, needs_upgrade, verify_password
    18→from ttrss.extensions import db
    19→from ttrss.models.user import TtRssUser
    20→
    21→api_bp = Blueprint("api", __name__, url_prefix="/api")
    22→
    23→
    24→def _seq(data: dict) -> int:
    25→    """Extract seq from request data — echoed in every response (CG-04, R08)."""
    26→    from flask import request
    27→
    28→    return int(data.get("seq", request.args.get("seq", 0)))
    29→
    30→
    31→def _ok(seq: int, content: dict):
    32→    return jsonify({"seq": seq, "status": 0, "content": content})
    33→
    34→
    35→def _err(seq: int, error: str):
    36→    return jsonify({"seq": seq, "status": 1, "content": {"error": error}})
    37→
    38→
    39→@api_bp.route("/", methods=["GET", "POST"])
    40→def dispatch():
    41→    """Single dispatch endpoint for all API operations (spec/03-api-routing.md)."""
    42→    from flask import request
    43→
    44→    data = request.get_json(silent=True) or {}
    45→    op = data.get("op") or request.args.get("op", "")
    46→    seq = _seq(data)
    47→
    48→    if op == "login":
    49→        return _handle_login(data, seq)
    50→    if op == "logout":
    51→        logout_user()
    52→        session.clear()
    53→        return _ok(seq, {"status": "OK"})
    54→    if op == "isLoggedIn":
    55→        # R09: content.status 1=logged in, 0=not logged in
    56→        return _ok(seq, {"status": 1 if current_user.is_authenticated else 0})
    57→    if op == "getVersion":
    58→        return _ok(seq, {"version": "1.12.0-python"})
    59→    if op == "getApiLevel":
    60→        return _ok(seq, {"level": 8})
    61→
    62→    return _err(seq, "UNKNOWN_METHOD")
    63→
    64→
    65→def _handle_login(data: dict, seq: int):
    66→    """
    67→    Authenticate user and create session.
    68→    Upgrades legacy SHA1 hash to argon2id on successful login (ADR-0008, R10).
    69→    Session stores user_id only — never pwd_hash (ADR-0007, R07, AR05).
    70→    Response includes session_id and api_level=8 (R08, spec/03-api-routing.md).
    71→    """
    72→    username = data.get("user", "")
    73→    password = data.get("password", "")
    74→
    75→    user: TtRssUser | None = db.session.scalars(
    76→        db.select(TtRssUser).where(TtRssUser.login == username)
    77→    ).first()
    78→
    79→    if not user or not verify_password(user.pwd_hash, password):
    80→        return _err(seq, "LOGIN_ERROR")
    81→
    82→    # Upgrade legacy SHA1 hash to argon2id on first successful login (ADR-0008)
    83→    if needs_upgrade(user.pwd_hash):
    84→        user.pwd_hash = hash_password(password)
    85→        db.session.commit()
    86→
    87→    login_user(user)
    88→    # AR05: store only user_id — pwd_hash MUST NOT be stored in session
    89→    session["user_id"] = user.id
    90→
    91→    return _ok(
    92→        seq,
    93→        {
    94→            "session_id": getattr(session, "sid", ""),  # Flask-Session sets .sid
    95→            "api_level": 8,
    96→        },
    97→    )
    98→

## Session Summary (2026-04-03)

TT-RSS PHP→Python migration spec-kit workspace created, refined (2 rounds adversarial self-refine), P0 ADRs accepted (1 round adversarial thinking), P1 ADRs accepted (1 round adversarial thinking with three-tier phase-aligned acceptance), and Phase 1a walking skeleton built and verified.

### Spec-Kit (built earlier same day)

**13 spec files** (162KB) in `specs/` + **15 ADR files** in `docs/decisions/`.
See `specs/` and `docs/decisions/README.md` for full index.

### P0 ADRs — ACCEPTED (adversarial thinking, unanimous convergence)

| ADR | Decision | Key Rationale |
|-----|----------|---------------|
| **0001** | **Variant D-revised** | Walking skeleton Phase 1a (1-2 days); 35 models via sqlacodegen; pluggy hooks from Phase 1b |
| **0002** | **Flask** | Native CSRF (Flask-WTF), sessions (Flask-Session+Redis), templates (Jinja2) |
| **0003** | **PostgreSQL + psycopg2** | Charter mandate; tsvector eliminates Sphinx; sync driver; pgloader for MySQL migration |

### P1 ADRs — ACCEPTED via Three-Tier Phase-Aligned Acceptance

Adversarial thinking pipeline: 3 divergent candidates (Accept-All, Challenge-Security, Minimal-Bundle) stress-tested via isolated critique + 3 author agents. All 3 converged to the same three-tier structure. Condorcet skipped per >80% overlap rule.

#### Tier 1 — ACCEPTED NOW (Phase 1a blockers + security mandates)

| ADR | Decision | Key Rationale |
|-----|----------|---------------|
| **0005** | **Option B: Manual analysis** | Manual analysis already complete (8 communities, 10 clusters). Option A (1-2 days) competes with Phase 1a. |
| **0006** | **SQLAlchemy ORM** (hybrid Core) | Blocks all model/query code. sqlacodegen + Alembic + factory_boy. |
| **0007** | **Flask-Login + Redis** | Blocks auth. Redis shared with future Celery. TTL replaces manual session GC. |
| **0008** | **Dual-hash gradual** (argon2id) | OWASP-recommended. No batch data migration. Clear SHA1 removal end state. Remediates spec-06 F1. |
| **0009** | **Fernet** (cryptography lib) | Misuse-resistant API. MultiFernet key rotation. Remediates spec-06 F3. Needed for Phase 1b auth_pass model. |

#### Tier 2 — Accept at Phase 1a EXIT GATE (Phase 3 blockers, clear frontrunners)

#### Tier 3 — Accept at Phase 2 EXIT GATE

- No SQLite anywhere — AR07; real Postgres via `docker-compose.test.yml` for all ORM tests

### Key Improvements from P1 Adversarial Review

1. **Three-tier phased acceptance** instead of accept-all — aligns with Variant D-revised discipline
2. **ADR-0005 resolved explicitly** as Option B — eliminates conditional "if time permits" ambiguity
3. **ADR-0009 promoted to Tier 1** — AGENTS.md Rule 14 mandates fixing HIGH-severity findings; model layer needs encryption approach for `auth_pass`
4. **Wrap-hash rejected** — OWASP password shucking risk, permanent SHA1 in hot path, batch migration required
5. **AES-GCM rejected** — nonce misuse catastrophic for solo dev; Fernet is the app-developer choice
6. **atoma rejected** — inactive project, 2.6K weekly downloads vs feedparser's 13M monthly
7. **All 10 spec-06 findings mapped** to accepted decisions or specific phases

    50→
    51→## Critical Rules
    52→
    53→### Storage Rules
    54→1. **NEVER** write files into `~/.claude/projects/*/memory/` — all memory goes to `./memory/`
    55→2. **NEVER** modify anything inside `source-repos/` — it is read-only reference
    56→3. **NEVER** store project specs, memory, or rules in `.claude/` — that dir is only for Claude-specific config (settings, skills)
    57→4. All specs, memory, rules, and artifacts go in the **project root** under their respective directories
    58→5. This ensures cross-platform portability (not tied to Claude's home directory)
    59→
    60→### Migration Rules
    61→6. Target Python code goes into `target-repos/` — this is where the migrated project grows
    62→7. Every spec document in `specs/` must cross-reference source files by relative path (e.g., `source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/classes/db.php`) rather than duplicating source code
    63→8. Specs may include **reasonable code examples** to highlight important architectural decisions, but must not be a copy of the source
    64→9. When migrating, always verify behavior parity against the source spec before marking a component complete
    65→
    66→### Source Traceability Rule (MANDATORY)
    67→10. **Every meaningful code element** (function, class, method, model, route, constant) in `target-repos/` **MUST** have a traceability comment linking it to its PHP source origin. This is a hard constraint — code without traceability comments must not be committed.
    68→
    69→    **Traceability comment format** (use the most specific match available):
    70→
    71→    ```python
    72→    # Source: ttrss/classes/feeds.php:Feeds::view (lines 45-120)
    73→    def view_feed(feed_id: int, view_mode: str) -> dict:
    74→        ...
    75→
    76→    # Source: ttrss/include/functions.php:catchup_feed (lines 1094-1237)
    77→    def catchup_feed(feed_id: int, cat_view: bool, ...) -> None:
    78→        ...
    79→
    80→    # Source: ttrss/classes/db.php:Db (singleton pattern)
    81→    # Python equivalent: SQLAlchemy engine via Flask-SQLAlchemy extension
    82→    db = SQLAlchemy(model_class=Base)
    83→
    84→    # Source: ttrss/schema/ttrss_schema_pgsql.sql (table ttrss_feeds, lines 38-72)
    85→    class Feed(Base):
    86→        __tablename__ = "ttrss_feeds"
    87→        ...
    88→    ```
    89→
    90→    **Match levels** (use the most specific that applies):
    91→    - **Direct**: `function → function` or `class → class` (e.g., `Feeds::view` → `view_feed()`)
    92→    - **Method-level**: `Class::method` → Python method (e.g., `RPC::mark` → `rpc.mark_article()`)
    93→    - **File-level**: When a Python module aggregates logic from a single PHP file (e.g., `# Source: ttrss/include/ccache.php`)
    94→    - **Multi-file**: When a Python module synthesizes logic from multiple PHP files (e.g., `# Source: ttrss/include/functions.php + ttrss/include/functions2.php (query building)`)
    95→    - **Schema-level**: For models derived from SQL schema (e.g., `# Source: ttrss/schema/ttrss_schema_pgsql.sql (table ttrss_user_entries)`)
    96→    - **Inferred**: When Python code has no direct PHP equivalent but was inferred from PHP patterns (e.g., `# Inferred from: ttrss/include/sessions.php (session validation pattern, adapted for Flask-Login)`)
    97→    - **New**: When code is genuinely new with no PHP source (e.g., `# New: no PHP equivalent (Alembic migration infrastructure)`)
    98→
    99→### Analysis Rules
   100→10. Use deep web research for any complicated architectural topic (PHP patterns, 3-tier architecture, ORM vs transactional script, etc.)
   101→11. For source code analysis dimensions (call graph, entity graph, etc.), consider using NetworkX and Leiden community detection
   102→12. Migration flow is driven by dimensions documented in `specs/10-migration-dimensions.md` — discuss and choose flow before starting migration
   103→
   104→### Quality Rules
   105→13. Preserve all functional behavior from the PHP source
   106→14. Fix known security issues during migration (SHA1→argon2id, prepared statements, etc.) — document deviations in specs
   107→15. Maintain spec-to-code traceability throughout the migration
   108→
   109→### Consistency Rule (MANDATORY)
   110→16. **When any status, decision, or phase changes**, update ALL locations that reference it in the same commit. This is a hard constraint — partial status updates create contradictions that compound across sessions.
   111→
   112→    **Mandatory update checklist** (run mentally before every status change):
   113→    - [ ] `AGENTS.md` — Architecture Decisions table (status column)
   114→    - [ ] `docs/decisions/README.md` — Decision Index table (status + priority columns)
   115→    - [ ] `docs/decisions/XXXX-*.md` — the ADR itself (Status, Date accepted, Deciders, Decision section)
   116→    - [ ] `specs/00-project-charter.md` — Solution Space table (decision + status columns)
   117→    - [ ] `specs/00-project-charter.md` — Requirements Traceability Matrix (status column)
   118→    - [ ] `specs/00-project-charter.md` — Cross-Reference table (if new ADR linkages discovered)
   119→    - [ ] `specs/10-migration-dimensions.md` — Recommendation Matrix (if flow variant affected)
   120→    - [ ] `memory/session_*.md` — session memory (current state for next session)
   121→

```
     1→# 00 — Project Charter
     2→
     3→Mission, Goals, Premises, Constraints, and Traceability for the TT-RSS PHP-to-Python migration.
     4→
     5→## Requirements Discovery
     6→
     7→Bottom-up analysis of the TT-RSS PHP codebase was performed across ten dimensions: architecture (spec 01), database schema (02), API/routing (03), frontend (04), plugin system (05), security (06), caching/performance (07), deployment (08), source inventory (09), and migration dimensions (10). Business rules were extracted in spec 11 and the testing strategy defined in spec 12. Findings from all twelve specs feed directly into the goals, premises, and constraints below.
     8→
     9→---
    10→
    11→## Mission Derivation
    12→
    13→Migrating TT-RSS from PHP to Python serves a terminal value: **reliable, secure, maintainable software that serves its users**. Python is the vehicle for achieving improved maintainability, security posture, and developer productivity — not an end in itself.
    14→
    15→---
    16→
    17→## Charter Specification (Mission, Goals, Premises, Constraints)
    18→
    19→### M — Mission
    20→
    21→**Deliver a reliable, secure, and maintainable RSS aggregation platform by migrating TT-RSS from PHP to Python, preserving all functional behavior while improving the technology foundation.**
    22→
    23→### G — Goals
    24→
    25→| ID | Goal | Litmus Test (changing it changes solution type) |
    26→|----|------|------------------------------------------------|
    27→| G1 | **Complete functional migration** — all TT-RSS features work identically in Python | If removed → no migration needed |
    28→| G2 | **Preserve API contract** — existing REST API and frontend-backend JSON contract unchanged | If removed → can break clients, different project |
    29→| G3 | **Preserve database schema** — existing data remains accessible without data migration (or with automated migration) | If removed → greenfield rewrite, not migration |
    30→| G4 | **Modernize security** — fix known vulnerabilities (SHA1, no prepared statements, SSL, etc.) | If removed → just a port, not an improvement |
    31→| G5 | **Containerized deployment** — Docker-based, CI/CD-ready | If removed → manual deployment, different ops model |
    32→| G6 | **Plugin system parity** — plugin architecture preserved with equivalent hook system | If removed → no extensibility, different product |
    33→
    34→### P — Premises (assumptions that must hold)
    35→
    36→| ID | Premise | If false → consequence |
    37→|----|---------|----------------------|
    38→| P1 | **Python ecosystem has adequate RSS parsing libraries** (feedparser, lxml) | Goal G1 impossible — need custom parser |
    39→| P2 | **SQLAlchemy can model the existing 35-table schema** | Goal G3 impossible — need different ORM or raw SQL |
    40→| P3 | **Existing frontend JS can work with any backend that returns identical JSON** | Goal G2 impossible — frontend tightly coupled to PHP |
    41→| P4 | **Team has Python web development competence** | All goals delayed — need training first |
    42→| P5 | **Source code is complete and representative** (no hidden dependencies outside repo) | Goal G1 at risk — missing behavior |
    43→| P6 | **The application's transactional script pattern can be preserved or improved in Python** | Goal G1 requires significant redesign |
    44→| P7 | **Background feed updates can be handled by Celery or equivalent** | Goal G1 (daemon) at risk |
    45→| P8 | **Existing .po/.mo locale files are compatible with Python gettext** | i18n breaks — need conversion |
    46→
    47→### C — Constraints
    48→
    49→#### Hard Constraints (violation = rejection)
    50→
    51→| ID | Constraint | Source |
    52→|----|-----------|--------|
    53→| C1 | **Never modify source-repos/** — read-only reference | Project rule (AGENTS.md) |
    54→| C2 | **All migrated code in target-repos/** | Project rule (AGENTS.md) |
    55→| C3 | **Behavioral parity** — same input → same output for all endpoints | Migration definition |
    56→| C4 | **Database compatibility** — must work with existing data (or provide automated migration) | Data preservation requirement |
    57→| C5 | **No secrets in repo** — config via environment variables | Security best practice |
    58→| C6 | **Spec traceability** — every migration phase references specs/ documents | Project rule (AGENTS.md) |
    59→| C7 | **Source code traceability** — every function, class, method, model, route in target code MUST have a comment tracing it to the PHP source origin (see AGENTS.md Rule 10) | AGENTS.md mandatory rule |
    60→
    61→#### Soft Constraints (violation = penalty, not rejection)
    62→
    63→| ID | Constraint | Penalty if violated |
    64→|----|-----------|-------------------|
    65→| C8 | **Prefer single database engine** (not dual MySQL+PostgreSQL) | Extra testing, complexity |
    66→| C9 | **Prefer established libraries** over custom implementations | Maintenance burden |
    67→| C10 | **Preserve plugin hook IDs and names** for documentation continuity | Minor confusion |
    68→| C11 | **Keep deployment simple** (single docker-compose up) | Ops complexity |
    69→| C12 | **Incremental migration** (avoid big-bang rewrite) | Risk of partial failure |
    70→| C13 | **Test coverage >= 80%** for migrated code | Quality risk |
    71→
    72→---
    73→
    74→## Solution Space (narrowed by 15 ADRs)
    75→
    76→The solution space was narrowed from broad options to concrete decisions via ADRs 0001-0015:
    77→
    78→| Dimension | Decision | ADR | Status |
    79→|-----------|----------|-----|--------|
    80→| Migration flow | Variant D-revised (Walking Skeleton + Hybrid Entity-then-Graph) | ADR-0001 | **accepted** (P0) |
    81→| Web framework | Flask | ADR-0002 | **accepted** (P0) |
    82→| Database engine | PostgreSQL only (psycopg2 sync driver) | ADR-0003 | **accepted** (P0) |
    83→| Frontend strategy | Keep existing JS, serve from Flask | ADR-0004 | proposed (P1 Tier 3) |
    84→| Call graph analysis | Manual analysis (already complete — 8 communities, 10 clusters) | ADR-0005 | **accepted** (P1) |
    85→| ORM strategy | SQLAlchemy ORM (hybrid Core for complex queries) | ADR-0006 | **accepted** (P1) |
    86→| Session management | Flask-Login + Redis (server-side sessions) | ADR-0007 | **accepted** (P1) |
    87→| Password migration | Dual-hash gradual (argon2id, upgrade on login) | ADR-0008 | **accepted** (P1) |
    88→| Feed credential encryption | Fernet symmetric encryption (MultiFernet key rotation) | ADR-0009 | **accepted** (P1) |
    89→| Plugin system | pluggy (hook registry) | ADR-0010 | proposed (P2) |
    90→| Background worker | Celery with Redis broker | ADR-0011 | proposed (P1 Tier 2) |
    91→| Logging | structlog | ADR-0012 | proposed (P2) |
    92→| i18n | Python gettext with existing .po/.mo files | ADR-0013 | proposed (P2) |
    93→| Feed parsing | feedparser library | ADR-0014 | proposed (P1 Tier 2) |
    94→| HTTP client | httpx (async in Celery workers only) | ADR-0015 | proposed (P1 Tier 2) |
    95→
    96→---
    97→
    98→## Anti-Patterns to Avoid
    99→
   100→These are specific to patterns found in the TT-RSS PHP source:
   101→
   102→| Anti-Pattern | Why Dangerous | Mitigation |
   103→|-------------|---------------|------------|
   104→| Replicate `db_fetch_assoc` iteration pattern | Verbose, error-prone manual row iteration | Use SQLAlchemy result sets and ORM queries directly (ADR-0006) |
   105→| Replicate `$_SESSION` global access pattern | Untestable, hidden coupling | Use dependency injection or Flask `g` / Flask-Login `current_user` (ADR-0007) |
   106→| Replicate dual-DB SQL branches (MySQL + PostgreSQL) | Double testing burden, divergent behavior | PostgreSQL only (ADR-0003) |
   107→| Replicate `htmlspecialchars()` calls | Easy to miss, leads to XSS | Use Jinja2 autoescape (on by default) |
   108→| Replicate `functions.php` / `functions2.php` monolith | 3000+ line god-files, impossible to test | Split by domain: `feeds.py`, `articles.py`, `users.py`, etc. |
   109→| Replicate singleton pattern for `Db` / `PluginHost` | Hidden global state, blocks testing | Use Flask extensions and dependency injection (ADR-0010) |
   110→| Gold-plating during migration | Adding features breaks behavioral parity | Strict parity constraint (C3); improvements come after migration |
   111→| Frontend rewrite during backend migration | Two moving targets, compounding risk | Keep existing JS in Phase 1 (ADR-0004) |
   112→
   113→---
   114→
   115→## Cross-Reference to Specs and ADRs
   116→
   117→| Charter Element | Primary Spec | Related ADRs |
   118→|-------------|-------------|-------------|

	function authenticate_user($login, $password, $check_only = false) {

		if (!SINGLE_USER_MODE) {
			$user_id = false;

			foreach (PluginHost::getInstance()->get_hooks(PluginHost::HOOK_AUTH_USER) as $plugin) {

				$user_id = (int) $plugin->authenticate($login, $password);

				if ($user_id) {
					$_SESSION["auth_module"] = strtolower(get_class($plugin));
					break;
				}
			}

			if ($user_id && !$check_only) {
				@session_start();

				$_SESSION["uid"] = $user_id;
				$_SESSION["version"] = VERSION_STATIC;

				$result = db_query("SELECT login,access_level,pwd_hash FROM ttrss_users
					WHERE id = '$user_id'");

				$_SESSION["name"] = db_fetch_result($result, 0, "login");
				$_SESSION["access_level"] = db_fetch_result($result, 0, "access_level");
				$_SESSION["csrf_token"] = uniqid(rand(), true);

				db_query("UPDATE ttrss_users SET last_login = NOW() WHERE id = " .
					$_SESSION["uid"]);

				$_SESSION["ip_address"] = $_SERVER["REMOTE_ADDR"];
				$_SESSION["user_agent"] = sha1($_SERVER['HTTP_USER_AGENT']);
				$_SESSION["pwd_hash"] = db_fetch_result($result, 0, "pwd_hash");

				$_SESSION["last_version_check"] = time();

				initialize_user_prefs($_SESSION["uid"]);

				return true;
			}

			return false;

		} else {

			$_SESSION["uid"] = 1;
			$_SESSION["name"] = "admin";
			$_SESSION["access_level"] = 10;

			$_SESSION["hide_hello"] = true;
			$_SESSION["hide_logout"] = true;

			$_SESSION["auth_module"] = false;

			if (!$_SESSION["csrf_token"]) {
				$_SESSION["csrf_token"] = uniqid(rand(), true);
			}

			$_SESSION["ip_address"] = $_SERVER["REMOTE_ADDR"];

			initialize_user_prefs($_SESSION["uid"]);

			return true;
		}
	}

	function make_password($length = 8) {

		$password = "";
		$possible = "0123456789abcdfghjkmnpqrstvwxyzABCDFGHJKMNPQRSTVWXYZ";

   	$i = 0;

		while ($i < $length) {
			$char = substr($possible, mt_rand(0, strlen($possible)-1), 1);

			if (!strstr($password, $char)) {
				$password .= $char;
				$i++;
			}
		}
		return $password;
	}

	// this is called after user is created to initialize default feeds, labels

	function initialize_user($uid) {

		db_query("insert into ttrss_feeds (owner_uid,title,feed_url)
			values ('$uid', 'Tiny Tiny RSS: New Releases',
			'http://tt-rss.org/releases.rss')");

		db_query("insert into ttrss_feeds (owner_uid,title,feed_url)
			values ('$uid', 'Tiny Tiny RSS: Forum',
				'http://tt-rss.org/forum/rss.php')");
	}

	function logout_user() {
		session_destroy();
		if (isset($_COOKIE[session_name()])) {
		   setcookie(session_name(), '', time()-42000, '/');
		}
	}

	function validate_csrf($csrf_token) {
		return $csrf_token == $_SESSION['csrf_token'];
	}

	function load_user_plugins($owner_uid) {

	function encrypt_password($pass, $salt = '', $mode2 = false) {
		if ($salt && $mode2) {
			return "MODE2:" . hash('sha256', $salt . $pass);
		} else if ($salt) {
			return "SHA1X:" . sha1("$salt:$pass");
		} else {
			return "SHA1:" . sha1($pass);
		}
	} // function encrypt_password

	// Auto-creates specified user if allowed by system configuration
	// Can be used instead of find_user_by_login() by external auth modules
	function auto_create_user($login, $password = false) {
		if ($login && defined('AUTH_AUTO_CREATE') && AUTH_AUTO_CREATE) {
			$user_id = $this->find_user_by_login($login);

			if (!$password) $password = make_password();

			if (!$user_id) {
				$login = $this->dbh->escape_string($login);
				$salt = substr(bin2hex(get_random_bytes(125)), 0, 250);
				$pwd_hash = encrypt_password($password, $salt, true);

				$query = "INSERT INTO ttrss_users
						(login,access_level,last_login,created,pwd_hash,salt)
						VALUES ('$login', 0, null, NOW(), '$pwd_hash','$salt')";

				$this->dbh->query($query);

				return $this->find_user_by_login($login);

			} else {
				return $user_id;
			}
		}

		return $this->find_user_by_login($login);
	}

	function find_user_by_login($login) {
		$login = $this->dbh->escape_string($login);

		$result = $this->dbh->query("SELECT id FROM ttrss_users WHERE
			login = '$login'");

		if ($this->dbh->num_rows($result) > 0) {
			return $this->dbh->fetch_result($result, 0, "id");
		} else {
			return false;
		}

	}

1. **`encrypt_password` in `functions2.php:1485`**: `return "SHA1X:" . sha1("$salt:$pass");` — The PHP format is `sha1(salt + ":" + password)` NOT `sha1(salt + password)`. There's a colon separator between salt and password!

I'm realizing I documented the SHA1X format incorrectly in my Python code — I wrote it as salt concatenated directly with the password, but the PHP actually includes a colon separator between them. The double-quoted string in PHP interpolates the variables, so `"$salt:$pass"` becomes the literal salt, colon, and password before hashing. That's the actual bug I need to fix.

Now I'm tracing through how the salt gets stored and used — the `encrypt_password` function with mode2=true generates the `MODE2:sha256(salt.pass)` format, and both the full hash and salt are stored in the database. But for SHA1X specifically, the stored hash includes the prefix but not the salt itself, which means the salt must be retrieved separately from the users table during verification.

Looking at my Python implementation, I'm splitting the stored hash as `SHA1X:{salt}:{digest}`, but that's not matching how it's actually stored in the database — the salt is in a separate column, not embedded in the hash string. So the stored hash is just `SHA1X:` followed by the 40-character hex digest — the salt isn't embedded in it at all. This means my `verify_password` function needs to accept the salt as a separate parameter, and I need to reconstruct the hash by computing `sha1(salt + ":" + password)` and comparing it to the stored digest portion. I'm realizing the salt isn't embedded in the hash string at all — it's stored separately in the `user.salt` column. <?php
class Auth_Internal extends Plugin implements IAuthModule {
	private $host;

	function about() {
		return array(1.0,
			"Authenticates against internal tt-rss database",
			"fox",
			true);
	}

	function init($host) {
		$this->host = $host;

		$host->add_hook($host::HOOK_AUTH_USER, $this);
	}

	function authenticate($login, $password) {

		$pwd_hash1 = encrypt_password($password);
		$pwd_hash2 = encrypt_password($password, $login);
		$login = db_escape_string($login);
		$otp = db_escape_string($_REQUEST["otp"]);

		if (get_schema_version() > 96) {
			if (!defined('AUTH_DISABLE_OTP') || !AUTH_DISABLE_OTP) {

				$result = db_query("SELECT otp_enabled,salt FROM ttrss_users WHERE
					login = '$login'");

				if (db_num_rows($result) > 0) {

					require_once "lib/otphp/vendor/base32.php";
					require_once "lib/otphp/lib/otp.php";
					require_once "lib/otphp/lib/totp.php";

					$base32 = new Base32();

					$otp_enabled = sql_bool_to_bool(db_fetch_result($result, 0, "otp_enabled"));
					$secret = $base32->encode(sha1(db_fetch_result($result, 0, "salt")));

					$topt = new \OTPHP\TOTP($secret);
					$otp_check = $topt->now();

					if ($otp_enabled) {
						if ($otp) {
							if ($otp != $otp_check) {
								return false;
							}
						} else {
							$return = urlencode($_REQUEST["return"]);
							?><html>
								<head><title>Tiny Tiny RSS</title></head>
								<?php echo stylesheet_tag("css/utility.css") ?>
							<body class="otp"><div class="content">
							<form action="public.php?return=<?php echo $return ?>"
									method="POST" class="otpform">
								<input type="hidden" name="op" value="login">
								<input type="hidden" name="login" value="<?php echo htmlspecialchars($login) ?>">
								<input type="hidden" name="password" value="<?php echo htmlspecialchars($password) ?>">

								<label><?php echo __("Please enter your one time password:") ?></label>
								<input autocomplete="off" size="6" name="otp" value=""/>
								<input type="submit" value="Continue"/>
							</form></div>
							<script type="text/javascript">
								document.forms[0].otp.focus();
							</script>
							<?php
							exit;
						}
					}
				}
			}
		}

		if (get_schema_version() > 87) {

			$result = db_query("SELECT salt FROM ttrss_users WHERE
				login = '$login'");

			if (db_num_rows($result) != 1) {
				return false;
			}

			$salt = db_fetch_result($result, 0, "salt");

			if ($salt == "") {

				$query = "SELECT id
	            FROM ttrss_users WHERE
					login = '$login' AND (pwd_hash = '$pwd_hash1' OR
					pwd_hash = '$pwd_hash2')";

				// verify and upgrade password to new salt base

				$result = db_query($query);

				if (db_num_rows($result) == 1) {
					// upgrade password to MODE2

					$salt = substr(bin2hex(get_random_bytes(125)), 0, 250);
					$pwd_hash = encrypt_password($password, $salt, true);

					db_query("UPDATE ttrss_users SET
						pwd_hash = '$pwd_hash', salt = '$salt' WHERE login = '$login'");

					$query = "SELECT id
		            FROM ttrss_users WHERE
						login = '$login' AND pwd_hash = '$pwd_hash'";

				} else {
					return false;
				}

			} else {

				$pwd_hash = encrypt_password($password, $salt, true);

				$query = "SELECT id
		         FROM ttrss_users WHERE
					login = '$login' AND pwd_hash = '$pwd_hash'";

			}

		} else {
			$query = "SELECT id
	         FROM ttrss_users WHERE
				login = '$login' AND (pwd_hash = '$pwd_hash1' OR
					pwd_hash = '$pwd_hash2')";
		}

		$result = db_query($query);

		if (db_num_rows($result) == 1) {
			return db_fetch_result($result, 0, "id");
		}

		return false;
	}

	function check_password($owner_uid, $password) {
		$owner_uid = db_escape_string($owner_uid);

		$result = db_query("SELECT salt,login FROM ttrss_users WHERE
			id = '$owner_uid'");

		$salt = db_fetch_result($result, 0, "salt");
		$login = db_fetch_result($result, 0, "login");

		if (!$salt) {
			$password_hash1 = encrypt_password($password);
			$password_hash2 = encrypt_password($password, $login);

			$query = "SELECT id FROM ttrss_users WHERE
				id = '$owner_uid' AND (pwd_hash = '$password_hash1' OR
				pwd_hash = '$password_hash2')";

		} else {
			$password_hash = encrypt_password($password, $salt, true);

			$query = "SELECT id FROM ttrss_users WHERE
				id = '$owner_uid' AND pwd_hash = '$password_hash'";
		}

		$result = db_query($query);

		return db_num_rows($result) != 0;
	}

	function change_password($owner_uid, $old_password, $new_password) {
		$owner_uid = db_escape_string($owner_uid);

		if ($this->check_password($owner_uid, $old_password)) {

			$new_salt = substr(bin2hex(get_random_bytes(125)), 0, 250);
			$new_password_hash = encrypt_password($new_password, $new_salt, true);

			db_query("UPDATE ttrss_users SET
				pwd_hash = '$new_password_hash', salt = '$new_salt', otp_enabled = false
					WHERE id = '$owner_uid'");

			$_SESSION["pwd_hash"] = $new_password_hash;

			return __("Password has been changed.");
		} else {
			return "ERROR: ".__('Old password is incorrect.');
		}
	}

	function api_version() {
		return 2;
	}

}
?>
```


## Assistant

<thinking>
Now I fully understand the PHP auth flow. Key findings:

1. **`encrypt_password($pass, $salt='', $mode2=false)` (functions2.php:1481)**:
   - No salt, no mode: `"SHA1:" . sha1($pass)` — unsalted SHA1
   - Salt, no mode2: `"SHA1X:" . sha1("$salt:$pass")` — salted SHA1, colon between salt and pass
   - Salt + mode2=true: `"MODE2:" . hash('sha256', $salt . $pass)` — SHA-256, salt+pass no separator
   
2. **PHP Auth flow in `auth_internal` plugin**: The system generates two hashes from the password—one unsalted and one using the login as salt—then for legacy users without a stored salt, it tries both hashes before upgrading to MODE2; for modern users with a salt, it validates using SHA-256 with that salt.

3. **Salt storage**: The salt is kept separately in the `ttrss_users.salt` column, not embedded in the password hash itself.

4. **Hash format breakdown**: Legacy unsalted hashes are plain SHA-1, legacy salted hashes use the username as salt with a colon separator, and modern hashes use SHA-256 with a stored salt value.

Now I'm realizing my Python implementation had several critical flaws — I was embedding the salt directly in the hash format, using the wrong salt for SHA1X hashes, and completely overlooking the MODE2 format that actually gets used after the first login. The `verify_password` function also needs additional parameters like the login name and salt to properly validate against these different hash formats.

Looking back at the earlier analysis, I see that CG-03's note about salt being prepended was incorrect — the actual behavior depends on the format: SHA1 uses no salt at all, SHA1X uses the username as the salt with a colon separator, and MODE2 uses a stored salt that's prepended to the password before hashing.

Now I'm implementing the `verify_password` function to handle each of these formats correctly, checking for the appropriate prefix and reconstructing the hash with the right salt mechanism for comparison.

The changes needed are substantial: I need to completely rewrite the password module, verify the user model has the salt column available, update the login handler to pass both salt and login credentials to the verification function, and fix the existing unit tests that are testing the wrong SHA1X behavior.

Now I'm going to systematically work through these fixes and add traceability comments throughout, starting by checking whether the user model already has that salt column defined.
</thinking>

The PHP stores `"SHA1X:" + sha1(login + ":" + password)` with the LOGIN as salt, and separately stores a `salt` column for `MODE2:sha256(salt+pass)`. My implementation invented an embedded-salt format that doesn't exist. Let me check the current model and fix everything:

**Tool Call: Read target-repos/ttrss-python/ttrss/blueprints/api/views.py**
Status: Completed

```
     1→"""
     2→TT-RSS REST API (/api/ — equivalent to PHP api/index.php).
     3→
     4→Protocol (spec/03-api-routing.md, R08, R09):
     5→  POST or GET /api/ with JSON body (or query params for GET).
     6→  Response envelope: {"seq": N, "status": 0|1, "content": {...}}
     7→  seq MUST be echoed from the request in every response (CG-04).
     8→  API level: 8.
     9→
    10→Auth (ADR-0007, ADR-0008, R07, AR05):
    11→  Login stores user_id in Redis session only — never pwd_hash (AR05).
    12→  Legacy SHA1 hashes are upgraded to argon2id on first successful login (ADR-0008).
    13→"""
    14→from flask import Blueprint, jsonify, session
    15→from flask_login import current_user, login_user, logout_user
    16→
    17→from ttrss.auth.password import hash_password, needs_upgrade, verify_password
    18→from ttrss.extensions import db
    19→from ttrss.models.user import TtRssUser
    20→
    21→api_bp = Blueprint("api", __name__, url_prefix="/api")
    22→
    23→
    24→def _seq(data: dict) -> int:
    25→    """Extract seq from request data — echoed in every response (CG-04, R08)."""
    26→    from flask import request
    27→
    28→    return int(data.get("seq", request.args.get("seq", 0)))
    29→
    30→
    31→def _ok(seq: int, content: dict):
    32→    return jsonify({"seq": seq, "status": 0, "content": content})
    33→
    34→
    35→def _err(seq: int, error: str):
    36→    return jsonify({"seq": seq, "status": 1, "content": {"error": error}})
    37→
    38→
    39→@api_bp.route("/", methods=["GET", "POST"])
    40→def dispatch():
    41→    """Single dispatch endpoint for all API operations (spec/03-api-routing.md)."""
    42→    from flask import request
    43→
    44→    data = request.get_json(silent=True) or {}
    45→    op = data.get("op") or request.args.get("op", "")
    46→    seq = _seq(data)
    47→
    48→    if op == "login":
    49→        return _handle_login(data, seq)
    50→    if op == "logout":
    51→        logout_user()
    52→        session.clear()
    53→        return _ok(seq, {"status": "OK"})
    54→    if op == "isLoggedIn":
    55→        # R09: content.status 1=logged in, 0=not logged in
    56→        return _ok(seq, {"status": 1 if current_user.is_authenticated else 0})
    57→    if op == "getVersion":
    58→        return _ok(seq, {"version": "1.12.0-python"})
    59→    if op == "getApiLevel":
    60→        return _ok(seq, {"level": 8})
    61→
    62→    return _err(seq, "UNKNOWN_METHOD")
    63→
    64→
    65→def _handle_login(data: dict, seq: int):
    66→    """
    67→    Authenticate user and create session.
    68→    Upgrades legacy SHA1 hash to argon2id on successful login (ADR-0008, R10).
    69→    Session stores user_id only — never pwd_hash (ADR-0007, R07, AR05).
    70→    Response includes session_id and api_level=8 (R08, spec/03-api-routing.md).
    71→    """
    72→    username = data.get("user", "")
    73→    password = data.get("password", "")
    74→
    75→    user: TtRssUser | None = db.session.scalars(
    76→        db.select(TtRssUser).where(TtRssUser.login == username)
    77→    ).first()
    78→
    79→    if not user or not verify_password(user.pwd_hash, password):
    80→        return _err(seq, "LOGIN_ERROR")
    81→
    82→    # Upgrade legacy SHA1 hash to argon2id on first successful login (ADR-0008)
    83→    if needs_upgrade(user.pwd_hash):
    84→        user.pwd_hash = hash_password(password)
    85→        db.session.commit()
    86→
    87→    login_user(user)
    88→    # AR05: store only user_id — pwd_hash MUST NOT be stored in session
    89→    session["user_id"] = user.id
    90→
    91→    return _ok(
    92→        seq,
    93→        {
    94→            "session_id": getattr(session, "sid", ""),  # Flask-Session sets .sid
    95→            "api_level": 8,
    96→        },
    97→    )
    98→

<system-reminder>
Whenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. You CAN and SHOULD provide analysis of malware, what it is doing. But you MUST refuse to improve or augment the code. You can still analyze existing code, write reports, or answer questions about the code behavior.
</system-reminder>
```

     5→def register_error_handlers(app: Flask) -> None:

**Tool Call: Read target-repos/ttrss-python/ttrss/crypto/fernet.py**
Status: Completed

```
     1→"""
     2→Fernet encrypt/decrypt utilities (ADR-0009, R11, AR11).
     3→
     4→The Fernet/MultiFernet instance is NOT instantiated here.
     5→It is created ONCE in create_app() from FEED_CRYPT_KEY env var,
     6→stored as app.config["FERNET"] (MultiFernet for key rotation per ADR-0009),
     7→and retrieved here via current_app.config["FERNET"].
     8→
     9→This ensures:
    10→- No key derivation in model code (AR11)
    11→- No env var reads at module import time
    12→- Testability via app fixture (pass a test Fernet in create_app(test_config=...))
    13→"""
    14→from flask import current_app
    15→
    16→
    17→def fernet_encrypt(plaintext: str) -> str:
    18→    """
    19→    Encrypt a string using the app-level MultiFernet instance (R11, ADR-0009).
    20→    Requires an active Flask application context.
    21→    """
    22→    f = current_app.config["FERNET"]
    23→    if f is None:
    24→        raise RuntimeError(
    25→            "FERNET not configured. Set FEED_CRYPT_KEY environment variable."
    26→        )
    27→    return f.encrypt(plaintext.encode("utf-8")).decode("ascii")
    28→
    29→
    30→def fernet_decrypt(token: str) -> str:
    31→    """
    32→    Decrypt a Fernet token using the app-level MultiFernet instance.
    33→    Raises cryptography.fernet.InvalidToken if the token is invalid or from a different key.
    34→    """
    35→    f = current_app.config["FERNET"]
    36→    if f is None:
    37→        raise RuntimeError(
    38→            "FERNET not configured. Set FEED_CRYPT_KEY environment variable."
    39→        )
    40→    return f.decrypt(token.encode("ascii")).decode("utf-8")
    41→

Now I have everything I need. Let me plan the changes:

**`ttrss/auth/password.py` — Complete rewrite:**

The PHP authenticate flow:
1. `$pwd_hash1 = encrypt_password($password)` → `SHA1:{sha1(pass)}`
2. `$pwd_hash2 = encrypt_password($password, $login)` → `SHA1X:{sha1(login:pass)}`
3. If `salt == ""` (old users): check against hash1 OR hash2
4. If `salt != ""` (modern users): `encrypt_password($password, $salt, true)` → `MODE2:{sha256(salt.pass)}`


5. The `verify_password` function needs to handle all these formats: argon2id for new passwords, MODE2 with sha256 for salted passwords, SHA1X with the login as part of the hash, and plain SHA1 for the oldest accounts.

Now I'm defining the function signatures — `verify_password` takes the stored hash, password, and optional salt and login parameters, then checks against each legacy format in order before determining if an upgrade is needed. I need to add `salt: str = ""` and `login: str = ""` parameters.

**`ttrss/blueprints/api/views.py`** — update `_handle_login` to pass `user.salt or ""` and `user.login`:
```python
if not user or not verify_password(user.pwd_hash, password, salt=user.salt or "", login=user.login):
```

- Remove the bogus "CG-03 regression" (embedded salt format doesn't exist)
- Add MODE2 test
- SHA1X should use login as salt with colon: `sha1(login + ":" + password)` 
- SHA1 tests are still correct

**Tests integration** — no change needed since test_user uses argon2id.

**Tool Call: Write target\-repos/ttrss\-python/ttrss/auth/password.py**

Diff: /Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/target-repos/ttrss-python/ttrss/auth/password.py
```
"""
Password verification and hashing (ADR-0008, R10, AR04).

Source: ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php:Auth_Internal::authenticate
        + Auth_Internal::check_password (lines 19-176)
        + ttrss/include/functions2.php:encrypt_password (lines 1481-1489)

PHP hash formats (from encrypt_password):
  SHA1:<hex>        — sha1(password), no salt, legacy unsalted (old users, schema < 88)
  SHA1X:<hex>       — sha1(login + ":" + password), LOGIN is the "salt", schema >= 88 without salt col
  MODE2:<hex>       — sha256(ttrss_users.salt + password), salt from DB column, current default
  $argon2id$...     — argon2id (Python migration: upgrade on first successful login, ADR-0008)

Important: SHA1X embeds NO salt in the hash string itself. The "salt" for SHA1X is the
user's login name, passed separately. The ttrss_users.salt column is only used for MODE2.

Verification order (mirroring auth_internal authenticate() logic):
1. argon2id  — upgraded/new passwords
2. MODE2     — modern PHP salted SHA-256 (ttrss_users.salt column required)
3. SHA1X     — legacy salted using login as salt with colon separator
4. SHA1      — legacy unsalted (oldest TT-RSS installs)
"""
import hashlib

from argon2 import PasswordHasher
from argon2.exceptions import InvalidHashError, VerifyMismatchError

# Source: ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php (argon2id is the Python upgrade target)
_ph = PasswordHasher()  # argon2id by default in argon2-cffi


# Source: ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php:Auth_Internal::change_password (new passwords)
# AR04: SHA1/MODE2 are verify-only. All new/upgraded hashes use argon2id exclusively.
def hash_password(password: str) -> str:
    """Hash a new password with argon2id. Never SHA1/MODE2 for new passwords (AR04)."""
    return _ph.hash(password)


# Source: ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php:Auth_Internal::authenticate (lines 19-140)
#         + Auth_Internal::check_password (lines 142-176)
#         + ttrss/include/functions2.php:encrypt_password (lines 1481-1489)
def verify_password(
    stored_hash: str,
    password: str,
    salt: str = "",
    login: str = "",
) -> bool:
    """
    Verify password against stored hash.
    Returns True if valid, False otherwise.
    Does not modify the stored hash — caller must call hash_password() + save after
    a successful legacy verify to complete the ADR-0008 upgrade.

    Args:
        stored_hash: value from ttrss_users.pwd_hash
        password:    plaintext password to verify
        salt:        value from ttrss_users.salt (only needed for MODE2)
        login:       value from ttrss_users.login (only needed for SHA1X)

    PHP source equivalents:
        argon2id: Python migration upgrade (no PHP counterpart)
        MODE2:    encrypt_password($pass, $salt, true) → "MODE2:" . hash('sha256', $salt . $pass)
        SHA1X:    encrypt_password($pass, $login) → "SHA1X:" . sha1("$login:$pass")
        SHA1:     encrypt_password($pass) → "SHA1:" . sha1($pass)
    """
    if stored_hash.startswith("$argon2"):
        try:
            return _ph.verify(stored_hash, password)
        except (VerifyMismatchError, InvalidHashError):
            return False

    if stored_hash.startswith("MODE2:"):
        # Source: functions2.php:1484 — hash('sha256', $salt . $pass)
        # salt is from ttrss_users.salt column, concatenated directly (no separator)
        digest = stored_hash[6:]
        expected = hashlib.sha256((salt + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
        return expected == digest

    if stored_hash.startswith("SHA1X:"):
        # Source: functions2.php:1485 — sha1("$login:$pass")
        # The "salt" is the user's login name. Colon separator between login and password.
        # The salt is NOT embedded in the stored_hash string — it comes from ttrss_users.login.
        digest = stored_hash[6:]
        expected = hashlib.sha1((login + ":" + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
        return expected == digest

    if stored_hash.startswith("SHA1:"):
        # Source: functions2.php:1487 — sha1($pass), no salt at all
        digest = stored_hash[5:]
        expected = hashlib.sha1(password.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
        return expected == digest

    return False  # unknown hash format — reject


def needs_upgrade(stored_hash: str) -> bool:
    """
    Return True if the stored hash should be upgraded to argon2id (ADR-0008).
    All legacy formats (MODE2, SHA1X, SHA1) require upgrade.

    Source: ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php:Auth_Internal::authenticate
            (lines 91-101 — upgrade to MODE2 on login; Python upgrades all the way to argon2id)
    """
    return not stored_hash.startswith("$argon2")

```

```
"""
Pure function tests for ttrss.auth.password (ADR-0008, R10, AR04).
No database required — these functions operate on strings only.
AR07-compliant: AR07 prohibits SQLite as DB substitute, not the absence of a DB
when none is genuinely needed.

Source coverage:
  ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php:Auth_Internal::authenticate (all hash format branches)
  ttrss/include/functions2.php:encrypt_password (lines 1481-1489)

PHP hash format reference (functions2.php:1481-1489):
  SHA1:<hex>    — sha1($pass), no salt
  SHA1X:<hex>   — sha1("$login:$pass"), login is the "salt", colon separator
  MODE2:<hex>   — hash('sha256', $salt . $pass), salt from ttrss_users.salt column, no separator
"""
import hashlib

from ttrss.auth.password import hash_password, needs_upgrade, verify_password


def test_hash_password_produces_argon2id():
    h = hash_password("testpassword")
    assert h.startswith("$argon2id$"), "hash_password must produce argon2id hash (AR04)"


def test_verify_argon2id_correct():
    h = hash_password("correcthorse")
    assert verify_password(h, "correcthorse") is True


def test_verify_argon2id_wrong():
    h = hash_password("correcthorse")
    assert verify_password(h, "wrongpassword") is False


# --- MODE2 tests (functions2.php:1484: hash('sha256', $salt . $pass)) ---

def test_verify_mode2_correct():
    """MODE2: sha256(salt + password), no separator. Source: functions2.php:1484."""
    salt = "abc123salt"
    password = "hunter2"
    digest = hashlib.sha256((salt + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    stored = f"MODE2:{digest}"
    assert verify_password(stored, password, salt=salt) is True


def test_verify_mode2_wrong_password():
    salt = "abc123salt"
    password = "correct"
    digest = hashlib.sha256((salt + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    stored = f"MODE2:{digest}"
    assert verify_password(stored, "wrong", salt=salt) is False


def test_verify_mode2_wrong_salt():
    """MODE2: wrong salt must not verify — salt is from ttrss_users.salt column."""
    salt = "correctsalt"
    password = "password"
    digest = hashlib.sha256((salt + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    stored = f"MODE2:{digest}"
    assert verify_password(stored, password, salt="wrongsalt") is False


# --- SHA1X tests (functions2.php:1485: sha1("$login:$pass")) ---

def test_verify_sha1x_login_as_salt_with_colon():
    """SHA1X: sha1(login + ':' + password). Source: functions2.php:1485."""
    login = "testuser"
    password = "hunter2"
    digest = hashlib.sha1((login + ":" + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    stored = f"SHA1X:{digest}"
    assert verify_password(stored, password, login=login) is True


def test_verify_sha1x_wrong_password():
    login = "testuser"
    password = "correct"
    digest = hashlib.sha1((login + ":" + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    stored = f"SHA1X:{digest}"
    assert verify_password(stored, "wrong", login=login) is False


def test_verify_sha1x_wrong_login():
    """SHA1X: wrong login must not verify — login is the salt for SHA1X."""
    login = "correctuser"
    password = "password"
    digest = hashlib.sha1((login + ":" + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    stored = f"SHA1X:{digest}"
    assert verify_password(stored, password, login="wronguser") is False


def test_verify_sha1x_no_embedded_salt_in_hash():
    """
    SHA1X hash string is 'SHA1X:{40-hex}' — the salt is NOT embedded in the hash.
    The old implementation wrongly expected 'SHA1X:{salt}:{digest}' (3 parts).
    Source: functions2.php:1485 — return "SHA1X:" . sha1("$login:$pass")
    """
    login = "admin"
    password = "password"
    digest = hashlib.sha1((login + ":" + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    stored = f"SHA1X:{digest}"
    # stored has exactly 2 colon-separated parts: prefix and digest
    parts = stored.split(":")
    assert len(parts) == 2, "SHA1X hash must be 'SHA1X:{digest}' — no embedded salt"
    assert verify_password(stored, password, login=login) is True


# --- SHA1 unsalted tests (functions2.php:1487: sha1($pass)) ---

def test_verify_sha1_unsalted():
    """Legacy unsalted SHA1 (oldest TT-RSS installs). Source: functions2.php:1487."""
    password = "legacy"
    digest = hashlib.sha1(password.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    stored = f"SHA1:{digest}"
    assert verify_password(stored, password) is True


def test_verify_sha1_unsalted_wrong():
    password = "legacy"
    digest = hashlib.sha1(password.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    stored = f"SHA1:{digest}"
    assert verify_password(stored, "wrong") is False


# --- needs_upgrade tests ---

def test_needs_upgrade_mode2_returns_true():
    salt = "s"
    digest = hashlib.sha256(("s" + "p").encode()).hexdigest()
    assert needs_upgrade(f"MODE2:{digest}") is True


def test_needs_upgrade_sha1x_returns_true():
    digest = hashlib.sha1(("user:p").encode()).hexdigest()
    assert needs_upgrade(f"SHA1X:{digest}") is True


def test_needs_upgrade_sha1_returns_true():
    digest = hashlib.sha1(b"p").hexdigest()
    assert needs_upgrade(f"SHA1:{digest}") is True


def test_needs_upgrade_argon2id_returns_false():
    h = hash_password("p")
    assert needs_upgrade(h) is False


# --- unknown format rejection ---

def test_verify_unknown_format_rejected():
    assert verify_password("PLAINTEXT:password", "password") is False
    assert verify_password("md5:5f4dcc3b5aa765d61d8327deb882cf99", "password") is False
    assert verify_password("", "password") is False
